    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer9896429570296356909">Tom Badgerlock has been living peaceably in the manor house at Withywoods with his beloved wife Molly these many years, the estate a reward to his family for loyal service to the crown.<br/><br/>But behind the facade of respectable middle-age lies a turbulent and violent past. For Tom Badgerlock is actually FitzChivalry Farseer, bastard scion of the Farseer line, convicted user of B</span>
  <span id="freeText9896429570296356909" style="display:none">Tom Badgerlock has been living peaceably in the manor house at Withywoods with his beloved wife Molly these many years, the estate a reward to his family for loyal service to the crown.<br /><br />But behind the facade of respectable middle-age lies a turbulent and violent past. For Tom Badgerlock is actually FitzChivalry Farseer, bastard scion of the Farseer line, convicted user of Beast-magic, and assassin. A man who has risked much for his king and lost more…<br /><br />On a shelf in his den sits a triptych carved in memory stone of a man, a wolf and a fool. Once, these three were inseparable friends: Fitz, Nighteyes and the Fool. But one is long dead, and one long-missing.<br /><br />Then one Winterfest night a messenger arrives to seek out Fitz, but mysteriously disappears, leaving nothing but a blood-trail. What was the message? Who was the sender? And what has happened to the messenger?<br /><br />Suddenly Fitz's violent old life erupts into the peace of his new world, and nothing and no one is safe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9896429570296356909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1031590201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1031590201" />
    <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence"><img alt="Mark Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1031590201?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Lawrence" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1031590201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7492759572784501932">Reading Robin Hobb makes me feel like I'm back in school ... or it would do if that were where I learned to write fiction. I have on occasion felt rather pleased with my writing, but reading Hobb's work always makes me realise I've got a long way to go.<br/><br/>Hobb's particular mastery is in characters and the relationships between them. No story is going to work in the long term unless the characters hold you, unless you care what happens to them. Hobb doesn't rely on shock or purple prose, she uses th</span>
  <span id="freeText7492759572784501932" style="display:none">Reading Robin Hobb makes me feel like I'm back in school ... or it would do if that were where I learned to write fiction. I have on occasion felt rather pleased with my writing, but reading Hobb's work always makes me realise I've got a long way to go.<br /><br />Hobb's particular mastery is in characters and the relationships between them. No story is going to work in the long term unless the characters hold you, unless you care what happens to them. Hobb doesn't rely on shock or purple prose, she uses the understated power in close observation and an intimate knowledge of her subject.<br /><br />In Fool's Assassin we're starting a third trilogy with characters that first came to the page 19 years ago. Many readers will have literally grown up with Fitz and the Fool, some others may have grown old with them. Two decades is long enough to see substantial changes in the readers, the characters, and the writer herself.<br /><br />This is a book that wouldn't be possible without the groundwork laid before. It builds on the history we have with these characters and exploits it. The story that we see unfold has echoes the story that has gone before. Like a piece of music it builds on themes, reflects earlier melodies, improvises around them, and plays an old refrain.<br /><br />Sections of the story that I can't describe for fear of spoilers hit particularly strong chords with me and were very moving, but whatever individual experience you bring to the book it's going to play on your heartstrings.<br /><br />This isn't a high adrenaline book, though there's plenty of tension. It's more subtle than that, a more reflective and slower-paced tale. Hobb works her magic though and I felt gripped throughout. A powerful, passionate book that takes #1 spot on my reading list this year.<br /><br />I've said in the past that I wanted to be careful not to wear out my characters' welcome. It can be an uncomfortable reading experience to fall out of love with a character, to grow bored with them. The lead character in my first trilogy, Jorg Ancrath, burned very bright and that intensity couldn't be sustained over a long series. With Fitz however I find that none of the enchantment has been lost and that it's not habit that keeps me following his story - it's because it's as strong and compelling as ever it was and a privilege to walk the pages with him.<br /><br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br />......</span>
  <a data-text-id="7492759572784501932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1830297717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1830297717" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830297717?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007444205" href="/book/show/25452013-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830297717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15208514255211306494"><b>A truly beautiful and poignant start to the last trilogy in <i>The Realm of the Elderlings</i> series.</b><br/><br/>Seeing that this is book fourteen out of sixteen in Hobb's <i>RotE</i> series and it’s also the seventh book that features Fitz as the main protagonist, with the exception of new characters, Fitz, and The Fool (<i>The Fitz and The Fool</i> is the name of the trilogy, after all), every other character I mentioned have a strong possibility of being considered a spoiler so I’ll refrain from doing so. Instead, I’ll expl</span>
  <span id="freeText15208514255211306494" style="display:none"><b>A truly beautiful and poignant start to the last trilogy in <i>The Realm of the Elderlings</i> series.</b><br><br>Seeing that this is book fourteen out of sixteen in Hobb's <i>RotE</i> series and it’s also the seventh book that features Fitz as the main protagonist, with the exception of new characters, Fitz, and The Fool (<i>The Fitz and The Fool</i> is the name of the trilogy, after all), every other character I mentioned have a strong possibility of being considered a spoiler so I’ll refrain from doing so. Instead, I’ll explain what makes this book stands out from the series and what makes this one of the finest books in the series so far.<br><br><i>Fool’s Assassin</i> is the first book in The Fitz and the Fool trilogy, which is also the last subseries within Robin Hobb’s <i>The Realm of the Elderlings</i> massive series. The storyline began approximately fifteen years after the end of Fool’s Fate, Fitz is now old and living in peace but his past is about to catch up to him and put everything he holds dear in danger, like always.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Time is an unkind teacher, delivering lessons that we learn far too late for them to be useful. Years after I could have benefited from them, the insights come to me.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I won’t lie that my expectation for this trilogy was VERY low. <i>Fool’s Fate</i> ending disappointed me and <i>The Rainwild Chronicles</i> stands near the top of the worst series I’ve ever read. That’s why I’m really glad that Hobb decided to continue Fitz’s story one last time with this trilogy—at least that’s what I’m assuming here—because this was simply spectacular.<br><br>This book in a way is a retrospect book, the majority of the book were spent on Fitz’s current daily life and him contemplating about his past and present. However, with the extensive knowledge that Hobb has created for the past books, Fitz’s contemplation became something truly delightful, poignant, and sweet to read. We have seen his past as a kid, teenager, adult, it’s time to see Fitz deals with older life now. This doesn’t mean that he has turned completely into a different character. Sure he has become wiser (a bit), but he’s still the same sulking and brooding Fitz we know and they’re all for many damn good reasons.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I was almost annoyed at her for spoiling my perfectly good sulk.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>The story direction obviously means—once again—that the book is almost completely zero of action sequences. I’m seriously glad for this, Hobb in my opinion is a not a good battle/action scenes writer, Hobb is always at her best when she dived deep into her characters’ personalities and thoughts. Reading her prose about Fitz contemplating about the passage of time and how age changed a person physically and mentally in this book turns out to be the best sequences she ever wrote so far; she could go on and on about this and I’ll devour it with joy.<br><br> <b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“When we are children, we believe that our elders know all and that even when we cannot understand the world, they can make sense of it. Even after we are grown, in moments of fear or sorrow, we still turn instinctively to the older generation, hoping to finally learn some great hidden lesson about death and pain. Only to learn instead that the only lesson is that life goes on.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Now, let’s get on to the best part of the book and what truly makes this book superb, the new character, Bee. I can’t emphasize this highly enough, Bee is an incredibly well-written character and I truly love reading about her. Just from this book alone, she has become one of the best characters Hobb ever wrote and also, she has a POV! Yes, that’s right, for the first time since <i>Assassin’s Apprentice</i>, this is the first time in Fitz’s series that Hobb included another POV other than Fitz, and this is a brilliant decision. I’ll be honest here, Fitz is a wonderfully written character but I’m not a huge fan of him, being inside his head for the whole trilogy can be tiring and sometimes annoying. Bee’s POV provided a dynamic and nice change of pace from Fitz’s POV that the series have sorely needed for a long time; it’s also fantastic to see other people’s thoughts on Fitz from another POV rather than only from Fitz describing what other people feel about him and dialogues.<br><br><b>Picture: <i>Fool’s Assassin</i> by Dominik Broniek</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522921827i/25328203._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Fool’s Assassin</i> is one of the best books within the entire series so far but it shouldn’t come as a surprise by now because from my experiences so far with Hobb, she’s on the top of her game with the beginning of her series. Her second book tends to suffer from the infamous middle book syndrome and the conclusion—with the exception of <i>Liveship Traders</i>—always fell a bit short of becoming amazing. However, looking at how the story went on in this book, this could truly be the first time the second book delivers a superior book in comparison to the first one for me; I still have to see if the rest of the series will make my opinion backfired on me or not. On to <i>Fool’s Quest</i>, only two books left now!<br><br><i>You can find <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/pat/1108-foolsassassin" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></b> and the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15208514255211306494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_808728589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/808728589" />
    <a title="Bob/Sally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally"><img alt="Bob/Sally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598307870p2/2224905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/808728589?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob/Sally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob/Sally" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally">Bob/Sally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer808728589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17545451004938528395">I can't remember the last time I felt so torn about a book, and so conflicted about a review. This was one of my most anticipated reads of the year, and I really wanted to enjoy it. In fact, compared to my usual reading pace, I spent a great deal of time in the world that Robin Hobb created - and while I did enjoy aspects of it, I have to be honest in that most of my time was spent waiting for aspects to enjoy. It's a testament to Hobb's writing (and to Fitz's legacy) that I was able to exhibit </span>
  <span id="freeText17545451004938528395" style="display:none">I can't remember the last time I felt so torn about a book, and so conflicted about a review. This was one of my most anticipated reads of the year, and I really wanted to enjoy it. In fact, compared to my usual reading pace, I spent a great deal of time in the world that Robin Hobb created - and while I did enjoy aspects of it, I have to be honest in that most of my time was spent waiting for aspects to enjoy. It's a testament to Hobb's writing (and to Fitz's legacy) that I was able to exhibit such patience. Looking back, the closest analogy I can think of is watching a chess game between tournament masters - fascinating, challenging, and admirable, but hardly riveting.<br /><br />Fool's Assassin may be labeled book one of the Fitz and the Fool Trilogy, but it's really an extended prologue of over 500 pages, followed by an opening chapter of about 80. That is to say there's a lot of talking, a lot of speculating, a lot of worrying, but not a lot of action. In fact, there are only a handful of scenes where anything of consequence takes place, and most of them are rushed together in those final 80 pages. It's hard to talk about them without getting into spoiler territory, but I will say the resolution of Molly's pregnancy is genuinely surprising, and those of you anxious for a reunion between the characters of the title will be waiting a very long time.<br /><br />Hobb's writing is gorgeous, as always, and it's easy to fall into the cadence and rhythms of her story. Initially, it felt like no time at all had passed since the last trilogy, allowing me to become lost in the world of Fitz all over again. It was truly marvelous. However, around the halfway mark I really began to feel the lagging pace, with the story slow going, but somehow still compelling. I genuinely doubt it would have worked if I weren't already so familiar with Fitz, and invested in seeing where his second life might take him. The problem is, Fitz wasn't Fitz. Yes, his personality was there, and I know Hobb was trying to show us how far he had distanced himself from his past, but I have a hard time believing he could become so lazy, so gullible, so careless, and so insecure.<br /><br />As for the other characters, that's a sore spot for me. Characters that we know and love, like Chade and Kettricken, are but pale imitations of their former selves. New characters, like FitzVigilant and Shun, are as shallow as they are annoying, while the most significant new addition (whose identity I refuse to spoil) is far too cold and awkward to ever embrace as a character, much less a narrator. Molly started out with some real potential, but soon became an extended plot device, and as fascinating as his (small) piece of the story is, we hardly get a chance to know the Fool.<br /><br />The opening scenes were fantastic, and I really expected the story to take off from there, but we're subjected to endless chapters of dancing, talking, dressing, shopping, dreaming, complaining, and musing. It took forever to come back to that potential and, when we finally did, it was a race to the finish with a cliffhanger that reeks of desperation. I will absolutely give the next book a read, but Fitz had damned well better return to his old self, and there had better be a significant payoff for all the time we've invested in tolerating that character/narrator I have been so careful not to spoil.<br /><br />Fool's Assassin is for hardcore fans only, and even then I suspect it will be something of a polarizing tale. Then again, maybe it's just me. The book does have a plethora of 5-star reads, so I'll be curious to see how the readers and reviewers I respect most react to the read.<br /><br /><br /><i>Originally reviewed at <a href="http://beauty-in-ruins.blogspot.ca/2014/07/fantasy-review-fools-assassin-by-robin.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Beauty in Ruins</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17545451004938528395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_994036230" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/994036230" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/994036230?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer994036230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7390891071414722472">Fitzchilvary Farseer, who has now adopted the name Tom Badgerlock, is enjoying his retirement; he has a fairly calm life compared to his assassin days. Most of the book is given over to him looking back on his youth and trying to move on from the past; it's a deeply introspective journey. Robin Hobb somehow managed to make the narrative flow so eloquently that I didn't realise that I'd stormed through the entire book in a day. <br/><br/><b> How does she do it? </b><br/><br/>I think it’s all about the wonderful characteris</span>
  <span id="freeText7390891071414722472" style="display:none">Fitzchilvary Farseer, who has now adopted the name Tom Badgerlock, is enjoying his retirement; he has a fairly calm life compared to his assassin days. Most of the book is given over to him looking back on his youth and trying to move on from the past; it's a deeply introspective journey. Robin Hobb somehow managed to make the narrative flow so eloquently that I didn't realise that I'd stormed through the entire book in a day. <br><br><b> How does she do it? </b><br><br>I think it’s all about the wonderful characterisation of Fitz and his relationship with his Fool, his Beloved. The two old friends have been separated for many years, and Fitz longs for the company of him. He is happy in his domestic life, but without the Fool there is a hole in his heart, a whole that could ever be filled with anything but the Fool. Not even a renewed relationship with his childhood sweetheart Molly Redskirkts could fill the gap nor could his strange daughter: Bee. He simply misses his friend and nothing but the Fool could end the emptiness. <br><br><i>"You never miss the water until the well runs dry."</i> <br><br>Robin Hobb leaves a trail that suggests that the Fool will return back to his Fitz, and this is what drove the novel forward. The domestic life of Willywoods is a mere front for separation between the two men. Fitz does his best; he keeps himself busy at home and protecting the outcasts his former mentor sends him. Also, his mysterious daughter keeps him very busy with her peculiar, yet familiar, nature. This keeps him busy; this keeps him distracted, but he still waits for his Fool, for his pack. <br><br><b>A strong bonding </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1437759499p8/1213621.jpg" width="400" height="277" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The relationship between the two is what makes this series so powerful and emotional, as the series matures so does their friendship. They have come a long way together, and have lost a great deal together. The two are attached to each other in a way that breaks the bonds of friendship and boarders upon the magical. They are connected. Without each other they would be nothing; they have saved each other from death many times; they are more than friends: they are the White Prophet and Catalyst. <br><br><i>"Undeserved forgiveness. Friendship defined." </i><br><br>Robin Hobb’s novels are superb. It is easy to become lost in her wonderful world. She is my favourite fantasy author. For me, she is just the best out there, at the moment, in her genre. No other writer I’ve come across can write friendships this deep and meaningful. This series gets better as it goes along. I am looking forward to seeing how it will all end, but I’d rather it didn’t end because then I could keep reading these books. It would be impossible to write a review for this book and not mention the ending; it has left me in suspense for a whole year. I think it was the best ending she has written so far, I do hope Fitz finds his Bee, and that the Fool gets his revenge. <br><br><b>A heartfelt five stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7390891071414722472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2630079419" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2630079419" />
    <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books"><img alt="Em Lost In Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522743986p2/11166121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2630079419?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Em Lost In Books" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books">Em Lost In Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780007444182" href="/book/show/22907376-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2010-19">2010-19</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2630079419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14106048566565509294">Long after the events of Tawny Man, when I thought all was wrapped up for good, Ms. Hobb came back and dropped this. And what a beautiful start she gave to this trilogy.<br/><br/>Tom Badgerlock is living in Withywood with his wife, all the kids grew up and left the nest to make their own life. Magic of Skill is keeping him young while his wife is slowly withering away into old age. He is enjoying his life but still can't stop drowning himself in self-pity at times. Those are darker times but he tries his </span>
  <span id="freeText14106048566565509294" style="display:none">Long after the events of Tawny Man, when I thought all was wrapped up for good, Ms. Hobb came back and dropped this. And what a beautiful start she gave to this trilogy.<br /><br />Tom Badgerlock is living in Withywood with his wife, all the kids grew up and left the nest to make their own life. Magic of Skill is keeping him young while his wife is slowly withering away into old age. He is enjoying his life but still can't stop drowning himself in self-pity at times. Those are darker times but he tries his best for the sake of his wife whom he loves dearly. It is Fitz we are talking about so trouble is never far, and here too trouble comes in form of a small package. Too bad Fitz didn't realize the real danger until it was too late. <br /><br />There are two other characters that grabs a lot of attention in this story. First is Fool, seriously anything related to Fitz is incomplete without him. They are the ultimate soulmates. No matter from which point they start their journey but one way or the other, their paths are bound to converge. For most part Fool we see in Fitz's memories and how he worried himself to know if the Fool is safe. Fool's appearance in the book is brief but once he is there it is all about him and the different paths world could take, all depend on, like every other time, on the actions of Fitz and the Fool (so the name of the trilogy is actually the exploration of the relationship of the two). <br /><br />About second character, I want to say a lot but every word will be a spoiler to the previous books. So I will try to keep it short about this pivotal character. This character is closely related to Fitz and all the while Fitz was worried about Fool, it was this character that was in real danger. Too bad it was too late when Fitz and Fool realized this. <br /><br />But for me the real star of the book was Hobb's writing. Even if the characters were frustrating at times, story was moving at a sluggish pace and yet I kept turning pages, gobbling down word after word. It was so beautiful. The pain, the sadness, the struggle, the waiting, it was all so real. Even if I felt that the story was a tad dull at times but I still won't change a thing about it. <br /><br />It was good to see Fitz and Fool again, only I didn't expect them to be this sad. Only if I could cheer them up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14106048566565509294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1010142413" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1010142413" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1010142413?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=alternative-pov">alternative-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=autobuy-authors">autobuy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1010142413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15171425559714901930"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434062411i/15172430._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Nothing warned me on that bright day that the darkest time of my life had begun."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b><u>03/05</u> : Reread of the week before finally summoning the courage to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23157777.Fool_s_Quest__The_Fitz_and_The_Fool___2_' title='Fool's Quest (The Fitz and The Fool, #2) by Robin Hobb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fool's Quest</a> (please don't break my heart) (please) (pleeeeeeease)</b><br/><br/><i>First of all, don't be fooled by the #1 here : <b>you CANNOT read this book if you haven't read the two first trilogies</b>. Trust me, it wouldn't make sense AT ALL, because it's Fitz's journey you're following here, and it started <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12479382-assassin-s-apprentice' rel='nofollow noopener'>in Assassin's Apprentice</a></i>.<br/><br/>If you're - even a</span>
  <span id="freeText15171425559714901930" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434062411i/15172430._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Nothing warned me on that bright day that the darkest time of my life had begun."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b><u>03/05</u> : Reread of the week before finally summoning the courage to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23157777.Fool_s_Quest__The_Fitz_and_The_Fool___2_" title="Fool's Quest (The Fitz and The Fool, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Quest</a> (please don't break my heart) (please) (pleeeeeeease)</b><br><br><i>First of all, don't be fooled by the #1 here : <b>you CANNOT read this book if you haven't read the two first trilogies</b>. Trust me, it wouldn't make sense AT ALL, because it's Fitz's journey you're following here, and it started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12479382-assassin-s-apprentice" rel="nofollow noopener">in Assassin's Apprentice</a></i>.<br><br>If you're - even a little - accustomed to this series, you must know that every chapter is introduced by a short excerpt from someone's memoirs - mostly <i>Fitz's</i>. That's why <b>I chose to write this review as an outlet for my memories linked to these amazing books</b>.<br><br>Fitz told his story. <i>This is mine</i>. Feel free to stop reading now if you can't stand personal reviews.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434062411i/15172431._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I started college for the first time, I screwed up. The truth is, I thought that I was ready to live in a dorm far from my family but I just... <i>wasn't</i>. Soon I began to ditch class more often than not, completely locked in my reading bubble (which is so ironic because I was in literature. I mean, I could slap myself). Of course my parents were worried and angry and you know what? They were right to be, but my 18s self would have never agreed with this, because basically? She was a fucking moron. But move on. Anyway, I managed to convince them that I needed to live out campus because ... well... less distractions let's say, and moved in a tiny apartment some months later. I still remember the loneliness I felt this first night, on my couch surrounded by blank walls. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434062411i/15172432._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I still remember saying myself that I was wrong and didn't make the good choice. I still remember feeling scared, so scared (don't judge - I come from a 4 children family and never ever knew how to deal with silence - I didn't know then, anyway)<br><br><b>This first night I grabbed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45107.Assassin_s_Apprentice__Farseer_Trilogy___1_" title="Assassin's Apprentice (Farseer Trilogy, #1) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Assassin's Apprentice</a> and never stopped reading</b>. This first night I was hooked by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a>'s astounding writing which flows so easily that you don't even realize that you just read 600 pages in one sitting. This first night was filled with <b>Fitz's despair, The Fool's wit, Chade's strange schemes and Regal's cruelty</b>. <br><br>I won't deny it, I ate these books up in a week, stopping only to eat and (sometimes) sleep. What can I say? <b>Fitz always had the power to draw me in, to make me <i>feel</i> his struggles, his doubts, his hopes</b>. Don't expect a perfect male-lead : It's <i>Fitz</i> - I mean, I didn't hide that he is my favorite character of all times but if you don't know him, you need to learn that Fitz is a whiny, heart-wrenching, lonely, <i>"I do mistakes for a living"</i> kind of character. But <i>oh, boy</i>. <b>How real he is. How incredible and complex the relationships are</b> in these books. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434062411i/15172433._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Jump a few years</i>. Picture a student in teaching, who barely has enough time to breathe, let alone read. Yes, it was a multiple year book slump. Yes, it was as horrible as it sounds. Now, imagine how I felt when I discovered that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a> had, in fact, written a new trilogy about my beloved Fitz <s>I felt dumb to not have learnt it earlier</s>. Of course I was ecstatic. Of course I was full of hope, love, but damn, how worried I was! And the truth is, I was right to be, in my opinion anyway. Because this ending? I cried for <i>hours</i> after this - don't get me wrong, I wasn't angry at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a> for the path she chose for Fitz, because this bittersweet ending? It was so <i>him</i>, he who manages to screw up relationship faster than I say <i>Wit</i>. But I digress. I remember the day I finished it, in the middle of nowhere, fishing on a lake with my boyfriend (who was fishing. Mostly, I read and make coffee. I'm useful like that). I remember saying that <i>it couldn't be the end. IT COULDN'T BE.</i><br><br><b>I'm so glad to have been right</b>.<br><br><s>Well, really, I'm always glad when I'm right, I mean, who isn't? Huh?</s><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434062435i/15172435._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Do not agonize about yesterday. Do not borrow tomorrow's trouble. Let my heart hunt. Rest in the now."</b>
</blockquote><br>If you're still with me, first of all : congrats. I'm not gonna lie, before starting this book <b>I was scared shitless : will this book be the one that would spoil the series for me?</b> Will I love it as much as the others? <i>Will I, will I...</i> <br><br>So, did this book so awaited disappointed me? <b>Not by a long shot</b>. From page one I was tearing up, smiling, from page one I felt like coming back home. Do you expect some full action-packed book? Oh, no, no, please don't. If you know <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a>, then you are aware that as a first book in one of her trilogies, you have to wait for things to settle down before expecting real action. Of course I was never bored because COME ON, IT'S FITZ, and as always, his insightful but <s>way to</s> late interpretations of the events of his life enthralled me. Anyway, I thought I should warn you : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a>'s books must be <i>savored</i>. In any case the pace definitely quickens in the second half and kept me captivated and yes, in awe. <br><br>However, what you <i>do</i> find are <b>incredibly multi-layered characters</b> (Can I say that I adored Bee and the changes she brings in Fitz? Yes? Also, this character evolution? Fucking perfect), <b>an intricate web of complex relationships, a beautiful and stunning writing</b>, and as always with this series, the need to be accepted for who you are despite your differences - <b>the excruciating journey that can be life</b>. Because what's Fitz story but the expression of perseverance despite all the darkness lurking, all the rejections he faced? <br><br>I don't care if the story can be seen as non eventful and boring - watch out, because loss, fear, sadness or joy can overtake you at any instant, suddenly and harshly as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a> masters it.<br><br><b>I don't care because I'm home, and I'm overjoyed to be</b>. This story is about family, the one we have and the one we create. And we readers are part of it, in a way.<br><br><i>Guys. GUYS!</i> I feel like crying. <br><br>► Because these books? I never want to finish them - I dread their end, and again, Robin Hobb proved me that I was right to do.<br><br><b><u>Edit</u> : Because you KNOW you want to read these books (please do), here's the order to respect :</b> (I know, this is SUCH a commitment!) <i>in italics, the books that aren't mandatory to read, but it's in the same world, and we understand things better^^</i><br><br>1)<u>
  <b>FARSEER TRILOGY</b>
</u><br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45107.Assassin_s_Apprentice__Farseer_Trilogy___1_" title="Assassin's Apprentice (Farseer Trilogy, #1) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Assassin's Apprentice</a> ★★★★★<br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68487.Royal_Assassin__Farseer_Trilogy___2_" title="Royal Assassin (Farseer Trilogy, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Royal Assassin</a> ★★★★★<br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45112.Assassin_s_Quest__Farseer_Trilogy___3_" title="Assassin's Quest (Farseer Trilogy, #3) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Assassin's Quest</a> ★★★★<br><br><i>2)<u>LIVESHIPS TRADERS</u><br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45100.Ship_of_Magic__Liveship_Traders___1_" title="Ship of Magic (Liveship Traders, #1) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Ship of Magic</a> ★★★<br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45101.The_Mad_Ship__Liveship_Traders___2_" title="The Mad Ship (Liveship Traders, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mad Ship</a> ★★★★★<br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45102.Ship_of_Destiny__Liveship_Traders___3_" title="Ship of Destiny (Liveship Traders, #3) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Ship of Destiny</a> ★★★★★</i><br><br>3)<u>
  <b>TAWNY MAN</b>
</u><br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68488.Fool_s_Errand__Tawny_Man___1_" title="Fool's Errand (Tawny Man, #1) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Errand</a> ★★★<br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45109.Golden_Fool__Tawny_Man___2_" title="Golden Fool (Tawny Man, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Golden Fool</a> ★★★★<br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45108.Fool_s_Fate__Tawny_Man___3_" title="Fool's Fate (Tawny Man, #3) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Fate</a> ★★★★★<br><br><i>4)<u>RAIN WILD CHRONICLES</u> (4 books)</i><br><br>5)<u>
  <b>THE FITZ AND THE FOOL</b>
</u><br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288321.Fool_s_Assassin__The_Fitz_and_the_Fool___1_" title="Fool's Assassin (The Fitz and the Fool, #1) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Assassin</a> ★★★★★<br>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23157777.Fool_s_Quest__The_Fitz_and_The_Fool___2_" title="Fool's Quest (The Fitz and The Fool, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Quest</a> (released in August 2015)<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/738417769?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20640707-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2762336-linette?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer738417769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10419110810909543149">Fitz, my old friend, how I've missed you. Sit, here by the fire, have a brandy and let us catch up.<br/><br/>This is how I felt coming back into Fitz's company after a decade apart. Reading this book felt like catching up with an old, dear friend. We've both changed, spent years apart, and yet as soon as I started to read the first paragraph it was as if we'd never parted.<br/><br/>Minor spoilers if you haven't read the earlier Fitz books:<br/><br/>This was a wonderful book. Fitz and Molly are living at Withywoods, quietly a</span>
  <span id="freeText10419110810909543149" style="display:none">Fitz, my old friend, how I've missed you. Sit, here by the fire, have a brandy and let us catch up.<br /><br />This is how I felt coming back into Fitz's company after a decade apart. Reading this book felt like catching up with an old, dear friend. We've both changed, spent years apart, and yet as soon as I started to read the first paragraph it was as if we'd never parted.<br /><br />Minor spoilers if you haven't read the earlier Fitz books:<br /><br />This was a wonderful book. Fitz and Molly are living at Withywoods, quietly and happily, with Patience. Chade is still up to his shady tricks in Buckkeep, along with Kettricken and Nettle. At first we are only concerned with some domestic problems - Fitz no longer allows the politics of the world near his home, family and quiet life. Fitz doesn't venture far from home in this first book, instead the excitement keeps coming to him, whether he wants it or not.<br /><br />Of course, the problems do not stay domestic or small...they never do for poor Fitz, no matter how he tries to hide and push away the world. We are introduced to some new characters and get to know them and care about them in the way Robin Hobb always makes us do. We meet one special new character, and oh I do like her. <br /><br />There is even a remnant of a certain wolf flitting amongst the shadows on occasion, watchful and wise. &lt;3<br /><br />The ending is somewhat of a cliff-hanger, and I'll forgive Ms. Hobb for that only because she is bringing more of my favorite Fitz my way and how could I possibly stay upset with her when she's doing that?<br />And in the words of a wise fool, 'Time is an unkind teacher, delivering lessons that we learn far too late for them to be useful'. I wish Fitz didn't have to learn so many lessons. <br /><br />I did figure out one of the major twists in this story fairly early on and was a tad frustrated that Fitz didn't, but just a minor quibble.<br />4.5 stars<br /><br />I received this ARC from Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_740637605" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/740637605" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4878104-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515345527p2/4878104.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/740637605?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/4878104-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553392425" href="/book/show/19288321-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kat by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3395391-daydreamer">DayDreamer</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=bouts-of-fangirl-craziness">bouts-of-fangirl-craziness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=everyone-liked-it-but-me">everyone-liked-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=robin-hobb">robin-hobb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=sweet-anticipation">sweet-anticipation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=a-bit-too-long">a-bit-too-long</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=meh-but-not-awful">meh-but-not-awful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=gotta-get-through-this">gotta-get-through-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=dude-where-is-the-plot">dude-where-is-the-plot</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer740637605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5816796526443223140">Fitz would say, “I’m sorry, I’m so sorry.” Hobb would say that 2 stars aren’t bad. Still, it is with reluctance and some trepidation that I slap 2 stars onto this book. These days, I don’t write many elaborate reviews anymore, but I feel that I owe an explanation here. <br/><br/>Before things gets heated, I will proclaim my undying love for most of Hobb’s works in the paragraph below, because that appears the custom among underwhelmed, and therefore apologetic fans. Feel free to skip the next paragraph in</span>
  <span id="freeText5816796526443223140" style="display:none">Fitz would say, “I’m sorry, I’m so sorry.” Hobb would say that 2 stars aren’t bad. Still, it is with reluctance and some trepidation that I slap 2 stars onto this book. These days, I don’t write many elaborate reviews anymore, but I feel that I owe an explanation here. <br /><br />Before things gets heated, I will proclaim my undying love for most of Hobb’s works in the paragraph below, because that appears the custom among underwhelmed, and therefore apologetic fans. Feel free to skip the next paragraph instead! <br /><br />Right. When I heard about this series I was overjoyed. Two decades after I’d discovered <i>Assassin’s Apprentice</i> in a second-hand bookstore and had fallen in love with Fitz and the Fool, I had not expected to meet them again. And so it was with a mixture of anticipation and sweet nostalgia that I waited for <i>Fool’s Assassin</i>. I first met Fitz during my turbulent early teens, and as he took me with him through his life, book after book, trilogy after trilogy, I felt like I grew up with him. I remember missing my train stop because I was too engrossed in his story. Like yesterday, I remember how I - sadly also in a train full of commuters - broke down in tears when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Nighteyes died <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Someone asked me if I was "all right?" Of course I wasn’t all right! And I refuse to write this down to my being an emo teen: like with Fitz, a part of me died too that day. But I read on. I marveled at John Howe’s cover art: his perfect portrayal of Fitz, and that cover of Fool’s Errand, that I could stare at like my girlfriends did at Peter Andre’s abs in his <i>Mysterious Girl</i> days. Soon after, I had the opportunity to meet Hobb in a Dutch bookstore and, fortunately for her, I was insecure enough about my English that I did not bring her an ode. I let her quietly sign my copy instead. Then the <i>Liveship Traders</i> trilogy came along, and I reread it 3 times, or maybe 4?<br /><br />This book I will not reread. <br /><br />After the initial excitement of being back in the Six Duchies ebbed away, I began noticing peculiarities. Niggles, that at first I could easily shrug off. Like how unlikely it was for Fitz to let a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[messenger with an urgent, personal message <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> wait by forgetting all about her, then simply ignoring her presence. And how odd that a man who was literally immersed in assassin’s practices and mortal danger since his early childhood, passively wondered about the sudden arrival of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[strangers at a party in his house, and allowed them to murder said messenger and leave blood trails <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> behind in his private rooms. Not to mention his lethargic approach when a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[new (brutally hunted!) messenger made clear what was at stake. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />That, I could write off to Fitz possibly having lost his “edge”, a fear that he and others expressed throughout the book. Stranger is that he only briefly considered the “suspicious” events, before re-immersing himself in his domestic, talcum-powdered dream with a slightly mellowed, yet still occasionally scathing Molly. <br /><br />What followed was a day-by-day account of humdrum, interspersed with Fitz’ life-weariness, angst for Molly’s ageing body and mind, and a longing for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[another child of their own <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. In self-indulgent pacing, Hobb explored these topics over the course of the next 500 pages, in-between padding involving clothes, parenting issues, and repetitive narrative questions that were echoed back and forth between the two narrators, all the while barely touching upon traces of a plot other than a sense of foreboding and...<br /><br />Repetitive clues. Look, I’m someone who usually blazes through books, devouring them as fast as I can. I’m therefore probably the last person to point out the culprit in a murder mystery. Then how is it possible, I ask, that a writer that I hold in such high regard due to her proven brilliance in weaving subtle hints and clues into a story, managed to insult my intelligence so this time? I was so disappointed in Hobb’s Fitz in this book. I found it unacceptable that in spite of an avalanche of clues - almost patronizing in their blatancy - Fitz was this blind to the gigantic elephant in the room: the fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[his daughter was a <s>Mary Sue </s>“white prophet”. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Man! I was so incredibly frustrated with Hobb’s choice to turn Fitz - if nothing else an admirable observer - into such a dense, oblivious character for the sake of her foreseeable, stretched-thin plot. I figured it out the moment the BLOODY <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[CHILD WAS BORN, COME ON NOW! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Ahem, excuse me.<br /><br />So to make matters worse, Fitz’ narrative voice felt distant throughout. I understood him being subdued and weary after his traumatic past. I did. What I didn’t understand was why he not only had to be morphed into a shadow of his former self, but also into a stranger. I mentioned how his training and skills - his “edge” - appeared to have vanished. Small examples that stood out: despite having experienced a similar childhood, he repeatedly told his <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[bullied daughter “Oh, they don’t hate you!”, like your average clueless parent <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in a silly children’s book. And he showed his belly like a submissive wolf whenever one of the women in his life scolded or threatened him - and Molly, Nettle, Shun, even Bee had in common that to varying degrees they ALL treated Fitz with disdain, contempt, and sarcasm. I couldn’t handle letting my ereader do a search for the number of times he grovelled, muttering how “sorry” he was, but it was a lot.<br /><br />Where’s Kyle Haven when you need him to smack some respect into that lot?:p<br /><br />Ah, those gorgeous <i>Liveship Traders</i> books! Were the many narrators in that series all beautifully fleshed-out characters with unique voices, in <i>Fool’s Assassin</i> the two new characters were cookie-cutter idiots (My guess? It's a transparent strategy to make their coming-of-age in the following books more striking). And Fitz and his <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[daughter (in many chapters a toddler still!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> sounded so alike that at the beginning of a new chapter it wasn’t always clear whose head I was in. Bee’s narrative voice was perfectly uninteresting and added zero oomph to the story, since she mostly described exactly the same daily grind as Fitz. A missed opportunity that’s so unlike Hobb... I despair.<br /><br />Anyway, only in the last 80 pages of this book did the pacing suddenly pick up, and did Fitz display some character when confronted with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[animal cruelty <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. However, soon it became clear that this scene and the following “fuss” at the inn all served as a set-up to make his <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[stabbing of the “beggar” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> a more believable action. Yeah well, that didn’t work, did it? Not only was his behavior bizarrely at odds with Fitz’ lethargic character up until that point, I found it a forced, inelegant twist unworthy of Hobb. <br /><br />I should stop, shouldn’t I? And I I will. But let me point out a few final, minor annoyances first: 1) what on earth was up with that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Wolf Father?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Either you kill off a character or you don’t. You’re not supposed to bring some warped version of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Nighteyes back to chat with Bee in times of need.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That’s only okay in pulpy PNR. Here, it was just lame and icky. And 2) due to the overall lack of plot I was extra annoyed with the little teasing story-lines that turned out loose ends:<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bee supposedly learning to fight with a knife, Bee chatting with that (finally, an intriguing new character!) cat, Lant supposedly being taught by Fitz and possibly becoming an apprentice, Fitz possibly bonding with that fierce horse...  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Everything crashed and burned in favor of the dull daily grind.<br /><br />BUT... I’m determined to end on an optimistic note! Friends mentioned that <i>Fool’s Quest</i> is everything <i>Fool’s Assassin</i> was not. I’m a quarter in and I agree. So far, I’m engrossed in what feels like an old-fashioned, classic Hobb again. I’m so relieved, I could cry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5816796526443223140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2010730590" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2010730590" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2010730590?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553392425" href="/book/show/19288321-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2017-shelf">2017-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fanboy-goes-squee">fanboy-goes-squee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2010730590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4005461408518887151">Wow.<br/><br/>I mean, WOW.<br/><br/>I've read something like nine, now ten of her books at this point and they were all epic doorstoppers split as trilogies, and this one may actually be my favorite of them all.<br/><br/>Why? Well, it wasn't because there was a ton of death and grief in it. Indeed, middle-aged retired Fitz having a well-deserved life with his childhood sweetheart and bringing a new winter baby into their lives was probably the sweetest damn thing the author could have done for him.<br/><br/>She writes it so well that </span>
  <span id="freeText4005461408518887151" style="display:none">Wow.<br /><br />I mean, WOW.<br /><br />I've read something like nine, now ten of her books at this point and they were all epic doorstoppers split as trilogies, and this one may actually be my favorite of them all.<br /><br />Why? Well, it wasn't because there was a ton of death and grief in it. Indeed, middle-aged retired Fitz having a well-deserved life with his childhood sweetheart and bringing a new winter baby into their lives was probably the sweetest damn thing the author could have done for him.<br /><br />She writes it so well that I don't even miss all the epic dragon battles or the battles with the Forged or the battle for the kingdom on the high seas, with Skill and Wit fighting together for once. No. In this case, it's introspection and memories and trying to put all the hard crap behind him and settling into the life of his dreams.<br /><br />Too bad he's aging slower than his wife and he fears that she's going mad because of a pregnancy that lasted two years.<br /><br />But what is the real kicker is the fact that she wasn't crazy.<br /><br />In fact, his kid has both the Wit and the Skill. <br /><br />This is where it gets really interesting, because we see this kid grow up with our favorite hero, the Catalyst without the White Prophet, and we as readers are making all the connections as Fitz does not, safe in his marital and familial bliss, even after his poor wife has died. On top of that, his daughter Bee is easily one of the most fascinating characters in the book.<br /><br />No, the thing is... this book is objectively sedate. The currents of being a dad, missing his old friend the Fool, loving his wife... all these things are written so well that it's gripping and fascinating, but as we keep feeling the tension build, knowing that something will inevitably go wrong, we're left hanging on the edge.<br /><br />Nearly the entire book is a setup. We know this. We're just reveling in a gorgeous span of time, giving Fitz the peace he'd always desired after having become the most deadly assassin and mass-killer of the land. <br /><br />I just didn't expect to be completely bowled over by this slow boil and the emotional reunion or the rest that immediately follows it. <br /><br />I cried. I stopped reading and I cried. That's the kind of effect this book had on me, and I generally don't cry with any books. I'm too used to plots and situations. <br /><br />This one caught me unawares. Hard. So. Ten stars. :)<br /><br />I'm gonna plow through all three of these doorstoppers in a row. :)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4005461408518887151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1381925520" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1381925520" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1381925520?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=favourite-book-ever">favourite-book-ever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1381925520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9619232782438225460">Reread on 19.04.17-21.04.17 - Still agree with everything I said below, and on the reread there's a whole load of things that I just adored spotting a bit earlier, now I know what's to come in this book and book #2. I am SO excited to go onto #3 when it's out, so I am now diving into the second on for a reread of that :) 5*s still :)<br/><br/>This is possibly my new favourite ever book and once again it's a book focused on Fitz Farseer and the Realm of the Elderlings and is written by Robin Hobb. Although</span>
  <span id="freeText9619232782438225460" style="display:none">Reread on 19.04.17-21.04.17 - Still agree with everything I said below, and on the reread there's a whole load of things that I just adored spotting a bit earlier, now I know what's to come in this book and book #2. I am SO excited to go onto #3 when it's out, so I am now diving into the second on for a reread of that :) 5*s still :)<br /><br />This is possibly my new favourite ever book and once again it's a book focused on Fitz Farseer and the Realm of the Elderlings and is written by Robin Hobb. Although Hobb intended to finish up Fitz's storyline with Fool's Fate I think that book and the exceptional amount of emotional turmoil it awoke within me (lots of tears and smiles throughout) proves that she knows this character and can return to him at any point seamlessly. I thought that I could accept the way that the Tawny Man series ended as it was so beautiful and tragic all at once, but after reading this I truly believe I would have been missing so much had I not been able to dive into this series later on because it is truly exceptional!<br /><br />What I love about Hobb is the characterisation she has built over so many long novels with Fitz and many other in the cast. I feel like I know Fitz so well and yet his story is constantly surprising and exciting in this tale. She's able to convince me not only that Fitz and his friends are real, but that I am right there with him and experiencing the pain, happiness and tragedies with him. Fitz's character growth across the entire Realm of the Elderling's series is the best character growth I've ever encountered in a plotline and I just have to say that the story is excellent too. Whenever I though I might have sussed something I knew I was being led along sneaky trails by Hobb and that when the real revelation came I was shocked and awed by how it all turned out.<br /><br />There are some very highly emotional scenes within this book which deal with tragedy, sadness, disability and other harsh topics, but Hobb's mastery over her world and characters means that these scenes cut you right to the core and make you cry along with the characters who you love so much. I couldn't have said where the story was going to end up at any point and I was so excited and hooked into it that I never wanted to stop reading it.<br /><br />We also get the introduction of another viewpoint character within this book which I think worked incredibly well. In all the other Fitz books we don't get to have any view but his and the messages and scrolls which appear at the start of the chapters, but seeing the new viewpoint of this book was excellent and added a whole other feeling of awesome to the book (Plus I LOVED the character we followed).<br /><br />This story is set about 15 years after the ending of Fool's Fate and I have to say it's exceptionally well written because it skips over a large chunk of time in the first half seamlessly. Often when you read a book which covers a long time in a short period of pages it can come off as 'easy and unconvincing' but I think that the way Hobb handled it was flawless and beautifully balanced.<br /><br />In terms of the story and how much I loved it I can;t begin to put it into words because truly it was exceptional in every way. By this point of the series we are fully absorbed and attached to the characters and seeing what befalls them over the course of this book just made me an emotional wreck by the ending! I was sat in bewilderment and astonishment at how emerged I had been in the story for the last couple of chapters and coming out of my book trance was tough and emotional.<br /><br />Also, this awoke some emotions within me that not many books do, not only tears but excitement, happiness, tenderness, love, bitterness and anger. So many moments which are basically flawless between the characters, and so much more information about a certain type of character who have been a mystery to the reader since book 1 in the Farseer Trilogy.<br /><br />In case you cannot already tell, I adored this book and it is definitely tied for my favourite book ever next to Fool's Fate. Hobb is definitely staking her claim in the world of Epic fantasy and dominating all my other favourite authors in terms of skill, quality and passion for the world and characters. I cannot wait to read book #2 in the series and then eagerly await book #3 being released (I might have a breakdown if it's not out in a year or so though) as I have no doubt it will be just as fabulous. I cannot wait to see what will happen next, and I will immediately be starting book #2! <br /><br />This is a 5* book for sure (although I would give it more if I could) and I would highly recommend starting at the beginning of the Realm of the Elderlings books and working your way through this fantasy that Hobb has convinced me must be real somewhere. Utterly incomparable - HIGHLY RECOMMENDED!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9619232782438225460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553392425" href="/book/show/19288321-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>
