<span id="freeTextContainer15441012598554870403">I've waited a very long time for this book to come out, 10 years in fact. I've read all 9 books several times and I don't think I ever really gave up hope that there would be another book after Fool's Fate. The last year I have barely managed to keep a lid on my excitement. Robin Hobb will always be my favourite author, her books are so beautifully written, they break my heart every time. I always have this nervous excitement that just builds and builds as I get towards the end of the book. <br/><br/>Fool</span>
  <span id="freeText15441012598554870403" style="display:none">I've waited a very long time for this book to come out, 10 years in fact. I've read all 9 books several times and I don't think I ever really gave up hope that there would be another book after Fool's Fate. The last year I have barely managed to keep a lid on my excitement. Robin Hobb will always be my favourite author, her books are so beautifully written, they break my heart every time. I always have this nervous excitement that just builds and builds as I get towards the end of the book. <br><br>Fool's Assassin started off a bit too slow in my opinion but then this often happens in the first book of a new trilogy and I was sort of prepared for that. I was never the biggest fan of Molly and was a bit disappointed that she featured in such a large section of the book. However, Fitz was as lovable as ever and as usual he was trying his best to juggle a million things at once although, again, as usual everyone was still on his back. <br><br>I really begrudged Bee at the beginning, I'm not a fan of children in books, I didn't want Fitz to be tied down with a child, I wanted him to be free to roam around frolicking with the Fool! But, Robin made me fall in love with Bee, she was such a tiny thing, wandering the passages of Withywoods on her own and I read these words after her bereavement and she just broke my heart. I now consider her up there with Fitz, Fool and Nighteyes.<br><br><b>
  <i>Bee looked like a brush for hoof oil when I saw her, a little stick all swathed in black with the fuzzy pale stubble standing up on her little head.</i>
</b><br><br>I was turning very page anxiously waiting for the Fool to appear, although unfortunately he doesn't turn up right until the end and even then I was pretty devastated, well completely devastated if I'm being honest. I just have to trust Robin and hope that the situation improves. If it doesn't I don't know what I will do. It's a shame I have to wait at least a year to find out. <br><br>Poor Fitz, things never go well for him and it seems like he is now about to start out on another huge quest, I only hope the Fool is able to tag along and keep him company.<br><br>One of my favourite quotes from the book.<br><br><b>She gathered her strength. <i>'What you called him?'</i> <br>She spoke in a learned tongue, without accent, only the dropped words betraying her.<br>I swallowed fear and regret. This was not a time to lie. <br><i>'Beloved. I called him Beloved.'</i></b><br><br>Hopes for the future are simply more of this and more of Wolf Father.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409076145i/10930531.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <br> </span>

<div id="review_741022463" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/741022463" />
    <a title="Neeta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6261945-neeta"><img alt="Neeta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501593813p2/6261945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/741022463?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neeta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neeta" href="/user/show/6261945-neeta">Neeta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer741022463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6308199792713502658">Upon hearing that Robin Hobb was finally writing the sequel I’d always hoped for, I was excited, but also wary as it’s not uncommon to find awful sequels for well ended book series.<br/>I’ll cut to the chase and tell you, I was definitely not disappointed. Hobb’s prose is as flawless and as wonderful to read as ever, easily sliding us back into Fitz’s life as enjoyably as in previous books.<br/><br/>Fitz is living the life he’d always dreamed of, with Molly by his side in the comfort of his family home at With</span>
  <span id="freeText6308199792713502658" style="display:none">Upon hearing that Robin Hobb was finally writing the sequel I’d always hoped for, I was excited, but also wary as it’s not uncommon to find awful sequels for well ended book series.<br />I’ll cut to the chase and tell you, I was definitely not disappointed. Hobb’s prose is as flawless and as wonderful to read as ever, easily sliding us back into Fitz’s life as enjoyably as in previous books.<br /><br />Fitz is living the life he’d always dreamed of, with Molly by his side in the comfort of his family home at Withywoods. Much of this book details his everyday life as a family man struggling to reconcile his past life as an assassin with his new home life, running an estate. The pace is much slower, and I can understand if some readers might feel frustrated by this, but I found I enjoyed it simply because of the detailed look we get into Fitz’s thoughts. I empathised with Fitz and was able to understand both his pleasures and pains. Idiotic Fitz makes a return too, on multiple occasions (he’s not Fitz without his bad decisions and rashness lol).<br />His thoughts were engrossing, and at times heart breaking. Some of his struggles were so ordinary and everyday, I think that most people will find that they can relate to something on a personal level. This is something I’ve always loved about Hobb’s writing, she could be writing about Fitz doing the laundry and can still manage to draw you in and make those pages turn as fast as if it were a scene in which Fitz were dying, all because of the realism and depth of her character’s musings.<br /><br />There is a second POV in this book, which was equally as gorgeously written as Fitz’s, but I won’t go into that ;) I think readers will enjoy this unique character and their POV as much as I did though. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Bee is now quite easily in my top ten favourite characters of this series. I kept imagining the Fool at her age, experiencing the same things as Bee, and my thoughts went (where I think Hobb intended them to go) straight to the questions: ‘Who taught the Fool about his dreams, and how did he get all the answers about the White Prophets that Bee has no knowledge of?’ Of course, by the end of the book we have some answers, as well as new mysteries to ponder. The Servants. I was hoping this new series would go into the Fool’s origins and it looks like that’s where we’re headed! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Onto a few negatives. While the slow pace didn’t affect my reading experience, there was a nagging little thought in the back of my mind going ‘when is hell gonna break loose?’, as you expect it will eventually when reading a Robin Hobb book. It took much longer this time round, and the action was surprisingly fairly limited throughout the book also. My second qualm is a spoiler: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The wait to meet the Fool again was excruciating! I understand why he came in so late but aargh! Would have loved a few more chapters with him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Lastly, being a fairly impatient person, I’m not too fond of cliffhangers and Fool’s Assassin ends with a big one.<br /><br />These negatives didn’t have an impact on my enjoyment of the book (obviously from my rating). It was still a page turner and a perfect return to the magic of The Six Duchies and my favourite characters. The writing is Robin Hobb at her best, expressive and thoughtful with detailed and varied characters.<br />I have some theories about where the story is headed and I’m incredibly excited. Book 2 promises to be explosive and full of magic. I hope the wait isn’t too long.<br /><br /><b>5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6308199792713502658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_977618602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/977618602" />
    <a title="Evik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32551863-evik"><img alt="Evik" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/977618602?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evik" href="/user/show/32551863-evik">Evik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer977618602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17500818535585090089">I received a copy of Fool's Assassin on Netgalley.com to read it and write an honest review. <br/><br/>I read the book only a week after I had finished reading the Tawny Man Trilogy so the idea and the general flow of Hobb's book was still fresh in my mind. I dived into the ARC with an open heart and open mind expecting to read about Fitz and his new life away from Buckkeep, but also about his new adventures and other exciting things.<br/><br/>I expected too much. 80% of the book covers their day-to-day life and Fi</span>
  <span id="freeText17500818535585090089" style="display:none">I received a copy of Fool's Assassin on Netgalley.com to read it and write an honest review. <br /><br />I read the book only a week after I had finished reading the Tawny Man Trilogy so the idea and the general flow of Hobb's book was still fresh in my mind. I dived into the ARC with an open heart and open mind expecting to read about Fitz and his new life away from Buckkeep, but also about his new adventures and other exciting things.<br /><br />I expected too much. 80% of the book covers their day-to-day life and Fitz coping with various stupid and boring events, for example dances, celebrations, which clothes to wear (there's entirely too much talk about clothes in the book. Seriously), what to buy and what to do. The book introduces another narrator which could be done better, especially if the new narrator told the reader ANYTHING interesting or important for a Fitz novel. <br /><br />The characters in the new novel are very superficial and empty. We get to know FitzVigilant and Shun but only as far as to know that they are both huge douchebags, and the only character development Shun receives is going from 'kinda annoying and self-absorbed' to 'omg-i'm-a-goddamn-queen-diva'. I swear I was more impressed by the random cat who wanted a basket and a blanket than by the characters that have been very well constructed in all previous trilogies. Even old characters like Chade, Dutiful, Elliania and Kettricken are somehow empty so that the reader does not get the feeling of them being really *there*. <br /><br />The plot is non-existent. Really, what plot? There is no plot! There's only about 500 pages of boring recounts of day-to-day lives of boring characters (the new narrator is very out of place), and the last three chapters that cover about 80 pages are the only interesting part of the book. If I had wanted to read boring books I'd stick with Bleak House. <br /><br />I was really really very disappointed with the novel. Not so much because the story did not go as I wished or imagined, but because it was BORING. No plot. Bad character development. Nothing interesting to read up to the last three chapters. And even then it ended on a cliffhanger when all previous trilogies did not. I'm still hoping to hear that all of this was a bad joke played on us by Hobb and that the actual novel will be different and actually worth of bearing the name of such an acclaimed and competent writer as Robin Hobb has continually proven to be.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17500818535585090089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_836056849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/836056849" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5327687-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336796868p2/5327687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/836056849?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/5327687-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5327687-erin?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5327687-erin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5327687-erin?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5327687-erin?shelf=summer-2014">summer-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer836056849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5081045340677884885">As someone who enjoys character-oriented fiction, Robin Hobb has always been a particular favorite. She manages to write with a depth and honesty that not many authors manage, and her character development is second to none. <br/><br/>The Farseer books have tracked Fitz's development from youth to adult, and in this trilogy, deeper into middle-age. I really, really enjoyed Fitz's voice in this book. It's rare to find fantasy from an "adult" perspective and <i>Fool's Assassin</i> is a treat, if only for this fact</span>
  <span id="freeText5081045340677884885" style="display:none">As someone who enjoys character-oriented fiction, Robin Hobb has always been a particular favorite. She manages to write with a depth and honesty that not many authors manage, and her character development is second to none. <br><br>The Farseer books have tracked Fitz's development from youth to adult, and in this trilogy, deeper into middle-age. I really, really enjoyed Fitz's voice in this book. It's rare to find fantasy from an "adult" perspective and <i>Fool's Assassin</i> is a treat, if only for this fact. While we see an older Fitz is the Tawny Man trilogy, he's marked by years of exile; here, he's coming off a decade of normality and happiness, seeming much steadier for it. Make no mistake - this is still the Fitz we know and love - but there's a maturity here that wasn't present in earlier books.<br><br>Robin Hobb is also fantastic at conveying emotion, and with it, bludgeoning your heart. I find her books to be emotionally devastating with a sort of understated deftness: Hobb's characters don't often die, but they suffer, and <i>Fool's Assassin</i> is no exception to this rule. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Molly's alleged dementia was handled with particular care and despite not being a huge fan of her character, her death crushed me. I also think Fitz and Bee's relationship is very well done - particularly that early awkwardness and Fitz's confusion at how to handle a daughter who isn't quite 'right'.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>This isn't an action-oriented book and is, in my opinion, the slowest book Hobb has written: things don't really kick off until the last 100 pages or so and it ends on a pretty big cliffhanger. This isn't really the first book in a trilogy, but rather, the first third of a story; much of what's told here is exposition and focuses more on characters, their relationships, and setting the stage for what's to come. This doesn't really impair by enjoyment of the story, but it is, in part, the reason I gave the book 4 stars rather than 5.<br><br>My other qualm <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[is that Fool doesn't show up until the end. His introduction is great, and he's present throughout in Fitz's thoughts, but I suppose I expected to see him a little earlier. The Fool is my favorite character and so I'm obviously a little biased here, so YMMV. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>There's a new point-of-view character introduced about halfway through. I won't spoil who, as that's a plot point in itself, but I was pleasantly surprised. While at first I was turned off by the idea of a Fitz book being narrated by anyone other than Fitz, I was won over almost immediately. This narrator is very different from Fitz and serves as an excellent counterpoint - I underestimated how interesting it is to read from an alternative perspective, and I expect exciting things to happen with this character come Book 2. <br><br>In terms of plot, I'm a huge fan of where this series seems to be heading. I initially had no idea what to expect from <i>Fool's Assassin</i>; while <i>Fool's Fate</i> emotionally devastated me, I thought the ending was a bittersweet yet perfectly fitting end to Fitz's story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In hindsight, the focus of this trilogy seems almost obvious: the Farseer trilogy focused on the Skill, the Tawny Man on the Wit, and this one - it appears - will focus on the White Prophets and the magic of prophecy. I can't begin to express how excited I am to have some questions answered, and I look forward to seeing some of the Fool's mysteries unravel. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>If you've come this far in Fitz's story, I don't doubt you'll enjoy <i>Fool's Assassin</i>. Those more enthralled with the intrigue and conflict in previous series' may come out a little disappointed, though I think there's still enough here to keep you hooked. <br><br>---<br><br>The Fool's Assassin.<br><br>The <i>Fool's</i> Assassin.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389537906ra/8038785.gif" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5081045340677884885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2333955122" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2333955122" />
    <a title="Lema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18145934-lema"><img alt="Lema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507843225p2/18145934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2333955122?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lema" href="/user/show/18145934-lema">Lema</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007444205" href="/book/show/25452013-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2333955122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15076100723814637230">[My critical brain says 4.5 stars, my heart says SCREW THIS GIVE IT FIVE]<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“Time is an unkind teacher, delivering lessons that we learn far too late for them to be useful. Years after I could have benefited from them, the insights come to me.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Say hello to the slowest book on earth that managed to captivate me from page one, because Robin Hobb continues to be an evil genius. I gotta say, after my disappointment with Fool's Fate (if you are interested in me ranting <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2318015077' rel='nofollow noopener'>click here</a>) I was very apprehe</span>
  <span id="freeText15076100723814637230" style="display:none">[My critical brain says 4.5 stars, my heart says SCREW THIS GIVE IT FIVE]<br><br><i>
  <b>“Time is an unkind teacher, delivering lessons that we learn far too late for them to be useful. Years after I could have benefited from them, the insights come to me.”</b>
</i><br><br>Say hello to the slowest book on earth that managed to captivate me from page one, because Robin Hobb continues to be an evil genius. I gotta say, after my disappointment with Fool's Fate (if you are interested in me ranting <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2318015077" rel="nofollow noopener">click here</a>) I was very apprehensive about continuing on with the series, would it continue to disappoint? or should I just stay along for the ride and accept whatever will be served to us?<br>I was already too far gone, The Realm of the Elderlings -with all the frustrations it caused me- will forever be in my very top fantasy series of all time.. I became so invested in Fitz and the Fool that they became real people to me. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522805359i/25320429._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="381" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A piece of warning though, and not just about this containing ZERO action, literally, but I feel I need to warn you all fans who reached this book, that the Fool doesn't appear until much MUCH later in the book. Aside from those two points, this is one of my top books in the series with Royal Assassin and Golden Fool being my absolute favorites. <br><br><i>
  <b>“I was almost annoyed at her for spoiling my perfectly good sulk.”</b>
</i> Classic Fitz throwing shade at himself :'D<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522803841i/25320337.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Glorious Fitz in all of his glory *swoon*</i><br><br>This is the book where I loved Fitz best, where his already multi-layered character acquired more complexity and depth, we see him here in a new light literally, as there are chapters that aren't in his POV and for the first time we get to see him as seen by an other. I won't say who's the other POV is to try to minimize spoilers.<br>My other favorite new character is Bee, I love that little nugget, she's almost as intriguing as the Fool and she's adorable and I just can't ahhhh *clutches heart*<br><br><i>
  <b>“I will always take your part, Bee. Right or wrong. That is why you must always take care to be right, lest you make your father a fool.”</b>
</i> <br><br>So long story short, I loved it to pieces, it was full of tiny emotional scenes here and there that would just suprise me out of the blue with punches to the gut in way only Robin Hobb has mastered. I'm currently deep into Fool's Quest, because Holy Shit THAT ENDING GUYS! it made up for the entirety of the slow-paced plot! I just had to run and start the second book IMMEDIATELY!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15076100723814637230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede">Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780553392432" href="/book/show/19481080-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer841989360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12921755760531830602">I have had two life-altering experience when it comes to fantasy, first reading David Eddings <b>The Belgariad</b> as a teenager and then reading Robin Hobb <b>The Farseer trilogy</b> in my early twenties. They made me love fantasy. So it was with a great pleasure to finally be able to read the first book in <b>The Fitz and The Fool Trilogy</b>.<br/><br/><i>In this book Fitz is living a happy life with Molly, raising her sons, living a peaceful life in the country. But when a messenger disappears, everything changes, although he</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12921755760531830602" style="display:none">I have had two life-altering experience when it comes to fantasy, first reading David Eddings <b>The Belgariad</b> as a teenager and then reading Robin Hobb <b>The Farseer trilogy</b> in my early twenties. They made me love fantasy. So it was with a great pleasure to finally be able to read the first book in <b>The Fitz and The Fool Trilogy</b>.<br /><br /><i>In this book Fitz is living a happy life with Molly, raising her sons, living a peaceful life in the country. But when a messenger disappears, everything changes, although he doesn’t know it yet, it will take some time before he realizes that.</i> And that’s how much of the plot I’m going to reveal. The rest is up to you to find out!<br /><br />Robin Hobb has written a fabulous book, a worthy follow-up <b>The Tawny Man trilogy</b> and I loved every page, every chapter was a truly joyous experience, it’s a book you read until your eyes can’t take in anything more and you have to sleep so you can continue reading the next day. It’s well written and intriguing to read and it’s never boring, even though there isn’t much action in the book. I was pulled into the story and the only thing that I didn’t like was reading the last chapter and knowing that it will be a while before the next book.</span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28542255-scarletine?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944190704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6173002081622206841">Rip the book in two, read the second half!<br/><br/>I’m sure we all know, as avid readers, how books can burrow into our hearts and have a profound effect on our lives. Tawny Man did that to me, and I thought the Fool got such a bad deal at the end. I approached Fool Assassin with much trepidation. I had a feeling my wish for a bit of much deserved love and tenderness for the Fool and ‘Big Gay love story’ between Fitz and the Fool would be dashed on the rocks. But the cruelty shown to our beautiful Belove</span>
  <span id="freeText6173002081622206841" style="display:none">Rip the book in two, read the second half!<br /><br />I’m sure we all know, as avid readers, how books can burrow into our hearts and have a profound effect on our lives. Tawny Man did that to me, and I thought the Fool got such a bad deal at the end. I approached Fool Assassin with much trepidation. I had a feeling my wish for a bit of much deserved love and tenderness for the Fool and ‘Big Gay love story’ between Fitz and the Fool would be dashed on the rocks. But the cruelty shown to our beautiful Beloved was shocking! <br />I began with the Audible audio book, because of the masterful performances by Paul Boehmer and Nick Taylor on the last two trilogies. It was a HUGE mistake. The narrator read as if he were reciting a shopping list. 8 hours in I could not take any more. It was very upsetting. I asked audible for a refund- IT WAS THAT BAD! I got the kindle book and read on.<br /> The first 12 chapters of ‘Fools Assassin’ could have been edited to three. I found it deeply indulgent, and upsetting that Robin Hobb thought dragging out Fitz and Molly’s domestic life was a good idea. There was NO PLOT, and this man doesn’t even read like Fitz. This Fitz couldn’t even be arsed to look for word of the Fool after TWENTY years of parting! WTF! Some friend! What a shit! He leaves the ball in the Fools court and smarts that the Fool has not seen fit to contact him, like a sulky child. It makes the depth of their past intimacy seem worthless and shallow. This Fitz isn’t the vital, intense, passionate Fitz that we knew and loved. His ‘peace’ has given him a lobotomy and I just wanted to bitch slap him.<br />For the first 12 chapters the masterful intimacy and beautifully interwoven relationships and storylines are gone and we are left with shadows of what could have been. The focus on the interminably repetitive and boring domestic relationship between Fitz and Molly at Withywoods for the first 12 HOURS!! Bored me close to giving up on the book. The Fitz of The Assassin/Tawny man trilogies would not have been satisfied with an ordinary life, no matter how he yearned for it. And what of the Fool? God, Robin Hobb really hates him. Never have I read a character that I loved so deeply, who was so deserving of love and tenderness, being destroyed so. She has taken his beauty, youth, his lithe body, his confidence, joy and light and put him through a mincer. The last 80 pages are an incredibly harrowing to read. Anyone who reads those pages and doesn’t weep openly has a heart of stone. A new Fitz and the Fool book could EASILY have been a masterpiece, but this is not! I will forgive Robin Hobb for the miserable first 12 chapters of indulgent twaddle, because the cliff hanger was superb. I look forward to her returning to form for the next book in the trilogy and I really hope she gives the Fool a break.<br /><br />My M/M Fitz and the Fool fan fic is great fun! Please take a look! <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://archiveofourown.org/works/2074695">http://archiveofourown.org/works/2074695</a><br />Part 2!<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://archiveofourown.org/works/2295674">http://archiveofourown.org/works/2295674</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6173002081622206841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1024995744?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1024995744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3294368204001876662">What a great book!<br/>The most striking thing, to me, about this work is how very well Hobb balances small, quotidian dramas with world-shaking events. She understands perfectly how, from an individual’s perspective (and especially, from a child’s perspective) the small things can actually be the big things. And her writing is good enough that even the small things keep the reader on the edge of one’s seat (although this is not to imply that big things aren’t happening here as well).<br/><br/>This is the seve</span>
  <span id="freeText3294368204001876662" style="display:none">What a great book!<br />The most striking thing, to me, about this work is how very well Hobb balances small, quotidian dramas with world-shaking events. She understands perfectly how, from an individual’s perspective (and especially, from a child’s perspective) the small things can actually be the big things. And her writing is good enough that even the small things keep the reader on the edge of one’s seat (although this is not to imply that big things aren’t happening here as well).<br /><br />This is the seventh big, fat book following the life of FitzChivalry FarSeer. Having followed the series from the beginning (as I have) will definitely enhance the reader’s experience – but I actually wouldn’t say it’s necessary to have read any previous volumes. Hobb is a master of drawing characters in bold yet sensitive lines that get a reader emotionally invested in a character with remarkable rapidity. Warning: if you read this one first, you’ll want to go back and read all the others!<br /><br />The events here begin some years after we last saw Fitz – he’s now known as Tom Badgerlock, and is a settled holder at the manor house of Withywoods. He’s achieved a certain level of domestic contentment – but, of course, one that is tempered by a number of issues. Looming large among those is his feeling of sadness and loss that his beloved Fool seems to have abandoned him for good. He is also disconcerted by the fact that, due to the side effects of magic, his cherished wife, Molly, is aging faster than he is. In addition, hoped-for children never materialized….<br /><br />Well, to see where things go from there, you’ll have to read the book. Falling into these pages feels like a long-awaited homecoming. This is, in every sense, a return to Hobb’s best writing. Don’t get me wrong – the Soldier Son trilogy was ok. The Rain Wilds chronicles are pretty good. But this series is the best. Even though there’s plenty of grief and violence here, somehow wrapping yourself in this book feels like curling up on the sofa with a warm, fluffy blanket.<br />And… like its predecessors, it’s nice and satisfyingly long….<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1063305059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1063305059" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9146810-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581734604p2/9146810.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1063305059?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/9146810-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780553392432" href="/book/show/19481080-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=z_archive17_read-2017all">z_archive17_read-2017all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=own-hardback">own-hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=own-ebook">own-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=z_archive17_read-2017books">z_archive17_read-2017books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=z_archive17_bought2017books">z_archive17_bought2017books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=z_archive17_read-2017fromshelf">z_archive17_read-2017fromshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1063305059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4491107186788564450">After being a bit disappointed in The Rain Wild Chronicles, I was super excited to get back into the world of FitzChivalry Farseer, and wow did I enjoy this book. Fool's Assassin reminded me a lot of Fool's Errand, the first book in The Tawny Man trilogy, but with the quality turned up. This is a character book first and foremost. The fantasy and action elements of Fool's Assassin is toned down in favor of a family dynamic that is just ravishingly good. Because the reader has lived with Fitz for</span>
  <span id="freeText4491107186788564450" style="display:none">After being a bit disappointed in The Rain Wild Chronicles, I was super excited to get back into the world of FitzChivalry Farseer, and wow did I enjoy this book. Fool's Assassin reminded me a lot of Fool's Errand, the first book in The Tawny Man trilogy, but with the quality turned up. This is a character book first and foremost. The fantasy and action elements of Fool's Assassin is toned down in favor of a family dynamic that is just ravishingly good. Because the reader has lived with Fitz for 6 other books before this and we know the background of this world with the Liveship Trader and Rain Wild Chronicles, this family focus really works. I am not going to get into the specifics of this book's plot because it would definitely spoil many of the other books in this series. <br /><br />The reason this book is so good is because Hobb's writing ability has become honed to a level that is some of the best in all of literature. Where the previous series' writing seemed lacking, this felt like she was really trying to impress, and it works. Hobb knows these characters so well, being inside Fitz's head is so effortless. The reason why these long series are so successful is because authors become some intimate with their characters that they are able to write them on a level that makes the reader believe they are real. Fitz and the other characters in this world are as real to me as most of the people in my real life, sometimes more so. <br /><br />I was really impressed that Hobb could surprise me as much as she did with this book. I was really excited to see where this story led because where I thought she was going to continue the story was not at all close. I have to reign myself in before I start sounding too much like a fan boy. If you read these books for anything other than the characters, you may be disappointed in this book. Even though the characters and writing is close to perfect, there are moments when I wanted something a little more exciting to happen. However, this is one reason why I love slow burn books, because when the excitement does happen, it really hits you hard. I definitely covered my mouth in shock a few times while reading this. I loved it and I can't wait to dive in book 2 soon. <br /><br /><b>5/5<br />22/25 Possible Score<br />4 - Plot<br />5 - Characters<br />4 - World Building<br />5 - Writing Style<br />4 - Heart &amp; Mind Aspect</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4491107186788564450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_749588177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/749588177" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/749588177?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/22877780-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer749588177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8615257874906914478">As an avid fan of Robin Hobb, especially her Farseer and Tawny man Trilogies, it was a pleasure to return to the Six Duchies and reconnect with Fitz and a whole heap of other familiar faces from the earlier books. And what about the Fool you say? Well we don't see him so much this book, unfortunately - but he does show up eventually and I imagine we will see a lot more of him going forward.<br/><br/>We catch up with Fitz some ten odd years down the track, happily married and retired at Withywoods. The sto</span>
  <span id="freeText8615257874906914478" style="display:none">As an avid fan of Robin Hobb, especially her Farseer and Tawny man Trilogies, it was a pleasure to return to the Six Duchies and reconnect with Fitz and a whole heap of other familiar faces from the earlier books. And what about the Fool you say? Well we don't see him so much this book, unfortunately - but he does show up eventually and I imagine we will see a lot more of him going forward.<br /><br />We catch up with Fitz some ten odd years down the track, happily married and retired at Withywoods. The story then quickly spans another ten or so years where Robin Hobb changes the narrative structure by introducing a second first person POV and from there alternating between Fitz and "Bee." Even though the title of the trilogy would suggest otherwise, this book focuses more on this new character, "Bee." Fitz pretty much remains the same old Fitz, and he doesn't get involved in much more than household politics - Fitz' focus is centred on Bee and Bee's focus is pretty much on centred herself as we see her growing up in her pre-teen years. <br /><br />So could one really call this a Fitz and Fool novel? Yes! Because Robin Hobb still ends up somehow funnelling the story to a point, a convergence in time where the Fitz and the Fool come together as White prophet and Catalyst to cast a pebble in the rutt to jolt the wheel of time on a new course. Or so I'm guessing because this book ends on a cliff hanger, which makes it very hard to rate when you don't know how a story will resolve.<br /><br />Still, I enjoyed being immersed in Fitz and Bee's life and the everyday happenings at Withywoods. This is, as we have come to expect of Hobb, a character driven book with all the dramatic tension coming from the relationships and dialogue between the characters. As such, how fans will take to this book depends very much on how they take to the new character Bee. If you like Bee, you'll end up loving this book. If you think Bee is just getting in the way of more of Fitz or the Fool - then you may not like it as much.<br /><br />As for me, I loved this book and I thought Ben Elliot did an excellent job as the audio narrator. I'm giving this one...<br /><br /><br />4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8615257874906914478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4736889284706023027" style="display:none">I am A big fan of Robin Hobb and FitzChivalry. Her books are so character driven that I feel I know Fitz inside out and so was slightly surprised to realise this is only the seventh book he has been in. So I think I need to read the rest of this trilogy to understand everything in this first volume of the Fitz and the Fool.<br /><br />I love the world that Robin Hobb has created and I loved revisiting it. <div id="review_838354389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/838354389" />
    <a title="Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24364577-monica"><img alt="Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394594885p2/24364577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/838354389?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monica" href="/user/show/24364577-monica">Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer838354389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7965224800539614978">This review was originally posted on Avid Reviews: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.avidfantasyreviews.wordpress.com'>www.avidfantasyreviews.wordpress.com</a><br/><br/>Robin Hobb is one of my very favorite authors, and she has had a long career full of excellent fantasy novels. When she announced that she would once more return to the Six Duchies in a trilogy that would follow FitzChivalry Farseer, Hobb fans everywhere rejoiced. This is her third trilogy featuring Fitz, and he has always been my favorite of her protagonists. I am extremely honored to be able to review the fi</span>
  <span id="freeText7965224800539614978" style="display:none">This review was originally posted on Avid Reviews: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.avidfantasyreviews.wordpress.com">www.avidfantasyreviews.wordpress.com</a><br /><br />Robin Hobb is one of my very favorite authors, and she has had a long career full of excellent fantasy novels. When she announced that she would once more return to the Six Duchies in a trilogy that would follow FitzChivalry Farseer, Hobb fans everywhere rejoiced. This is her third trilogy featuring Fitz, and he has always been my favorite of her protagonists. I am extremely honored to be able to review the first novel in the new Fitz and Fool series, Fool’s Assassin. Since this novel is a continuation of a long established story line, I would strongly recommend first reading Hobb’s other Fitz series, starting with Assassin’s Apprentice.<br /><br />Fool’s Assassin begins by dropping the reader into the middle of Fitz’s happy retirement from the intrigue of the Farseer line. It has been approximately ten years since the events that took place in Fool’s Fate, and everyone but Fitz’s closest friends and family believe him to be dead. He is now known as Tom Badgerlock, and he lives a peaceful life in the manor at Withywoods with his wife Molly. But Fitz can never fully escape his turbulent past as an assassin for the throne, and a bastard of the Farseer line. One Winterfest night a messenger arrives for Fitz, only to disappear from his own household before delivering the message, leaving nothing but a trail of blood. Suddenly the violence of Fitz’s past is brought painfully to the present, and peace of his retirement is gone for good.<br /><br />This novel has less action and adventure than Hobb’s other stories, yet her writing is so strong she still manages to engage the reader enough that it is hard to put Fool’s Assassin down. Though it is not a hugely eventful start to a new series, it leaves the reader completely on the hook, and promises an ambitious story for Fitz’s future.<br /><br />The true magic of Hobb’s writing is how she makes the reader care for her characters. Even the everyday events of a Fitz’s life are fascinating, and his struggles can easily break the reader’s heart. The introduction of a new character close to Fitz’s heart serves to engage the reader deeper in the story than ever before, and creates a fascinating dynamic that makes this novel truly great.<br /><br />Hobb is tougher on her characters than any other author I know, and her stories serve to remind us that good does not always triumph and a greater meaning and purpose is not often revealed. She emphasizes the journey of her character’s lives rather than the destination, and this is what really makes her novel’s stand out. If you are looking for a fast paced and lighthearted read, I advise you to look elsewhere. But if you are looking for a story that will make you feel deeply for its characters, or a glimpse of a detailed and vast world filled with mysterious magic, then Hobb’s novels are definitely for you. Long time readers of Hobb may be slightly disappointed about the lack of epic adventure in Fool’s Assassin, but they will be mollified by the beautiful story that Hobb weaves, and the promise of greater adventures to come.<br /><br />Overall, I would rate this book 8/10.<br /><br />I received a copy of this novel from Netgalley and the publisher in return for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7965224800539614978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_738522026" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/738522026" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/738522026?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/22877780-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=sff-audio">sff-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=elderlings">elderlings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer738522026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1324423866183605167"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I enjoyed it, though not as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45108.Fool_s_Fate__Tawny_Man___3_' title='Fool's Fate (Tawny Man, #3) by Robin Hobb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fool's Fate</a>, and if anything it's heightened my sense of dread that this trilogy will ruin that book's ending.<br/><br/><b>NOTE:</b> I always strive to write spoiler free reviews, but this one may fall a little short. Since people may be used to that from me I wanted to give a little warning. Some of my comments about the book as a whole may be considered spoilery by those like me who are especially sensitive to them. I don't talk about plot at all, but some</span>
  <span id="freeText1324423866183605167" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I enjoyed it, though not as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45108.Fool_s_Fate__Tawny_Man___3_" title="Fool's Fate (Tawny Man, #3) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Fate</a>, and if anything it's heightened my sense of dread that this trilogy will ruin that book's ending.<br /><br /><b>NOTE:</b> I always strive to write spoiler free reviews, but this one may fall a little short. Since people may be used to that from me I wanted to give a little warning. Some of my comments about the book as a whole may be considered spoilery by those like me who are especially sensitive to them. I don't talk about plot at all, but some of my comments about the characters/book structure may affect your reading and I'd hate to do that to someone.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> I never planned to do this one in audio. I've done the other 13 books in Ms. Hobb's Elderling series in text and pre-ordered the hardcover of this at least 6 months in advance. But I got offered to do the audio a week before the book came out and I had a hard time passing it up.<br /><br />I really didn't like Elliot Hill much at first. He grew on me by the end though. I don't normally hear characters speaking in my head as I read and haven't had any issue listening to books I had previously read and finding the voices wrong.<br /><br />I did here for some reason. Fitz just didn't sound right to me. Same thing with Molly. Bee seemed fine, but really she sounded almost like Molly. I liked his voice for Chade though.<br /><br />Mr. Hill does a few voices and accents and does a fine job of it. It just took me a very long time to get used to. By the end though I seemed to get over it. I likely won't do the audio again unless I get another review copy, but I'd guess many people won't have the same issues I did with it.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />When I first heard confirmation that the rumors of a new Fitz and Fool series were true, I was full of mixed emotions. I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45108.Fool_s_Fate__Tawny_Man___3_" title="Fool's Fate (Tawny Man, #3) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Fate</a> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404258538" rel="nofollow noopener">My Review</a>). I've enjoyed all of Ms. Hobb's books but that's the only one I've given 5 stars too. I was just so satisfied with how it ended. Sure there were questions, but all the big things were resolved.<br /><br />So would this book ruin my favorite book? Well not yet, but it certainly hasn't alleviated my fears that the events of this trilogy won't tarnish things for me.<br /><br />Like many books by Ms. Hobb, things start out slow. I don't mean that in a negative way however. Somehow she is able to write in such a way that I don't mind the day to day life of her books. Despite my trepidation, it just felt nice to be back with characters I love. If you're looking for a lot of action or a flashy start, you'll be disappointed. I imagine that anyone picking up this book is already going to be a Robin Hobb fan and used to her style though.<br /><br />More than anything, Ms. Hobb's writing is able to evoke strong emotions in me as I read. Love, anger, happiness, frustration. Few other authors can make me despise a new character so quickly or completely. Similarly Fitz continues to frustrate me with the way he does things in a way that is just all too human. Often times the protagonist in a fantasy book faces external adversity and rises to the occasion. Meanwhile Fitz is frequently his own worst enemy. Poor Ms. Hobb loves putting him through the ringer too, and this book is no different.<br /><br />I had three issues with this book costing it that fifth. The first one I suspect many long-time Hobb fans will share. The other two may largely depend on the reader.<br /><br />The series is called Fitz &amp; Fool. The book is called Fool's Assassin. So why did it take so long for us to see the Fool? Sure he's mentioned often enough, but I want to spend time with him just as I am spending time with Fitz. So far this series seems a lot more like Farseer than Tawny Man in that regard.<br /><br />The second thing was the addition of a POV besides Fitz. I guess I'm a very jealous reader. I originally hoped it was a one off thing early in the book, but when it turned out to be a regular thing it bothered me. I felt robbed of time I could be spending with Fitz. By the end of the book it grew on me and I came to look forward to those chapters nearly as much as I did the Fitz ones.<br /><br />The final issue I had was the ending. I know this is the first book of a trilogy, but I hate cliffhanger type endings, and this one seemed pretty bad to me. If you're the type of person who hates waiting for the next book, you may be better off waiting until the final book is either published or has a release date. It's going to a be a LONG wait for me until book 2.<br /><br />Overall I really liked, but didn't love this book. I'm still pretty nervous about what may happen next. I think that above all shows how great a writer Ms. Hobb is to fill me with both a sense of anticipation and dread for the next book in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1324423866183605167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_904502404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904502404" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9595345-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362241942p2/9595345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/904502404?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/9595345-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007444175" href="/book/show/18658063-fool-s-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9595345-lisa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer904502404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7244860232399432833">Review Posted from TenaciousReader: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.tenaciousreader.com/2014/07/15/fools-assassin-by-robin-hobb/'>http://www.tenaciousreader.com/2014/0...</a><br/><br/>Confession time. I am obviously a cruel and selfish reader. Why? I’m selfish because I so longed for another story of Fitz and Fool, another book to spend my time immersed in their world. And yet I feel cruel because I know how these stories go. Poor Fitz, things never fare well for him. So to wish for more stories, I almost feel like I am intruding on his peace, and wishing him more pain. I love Fitz, how can I wish his</span>
  <span id="freeText7244860232399432833" style="display:none">Review Posted from TenaciousReader: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.tenaciousreader.com/2014/07/15/fools-assassin-by-robin-hobb/">http://www.tenaciousreader.com/2014/0...</a><br /><br />Confession time. I am obviously a cruel and selfish reader. Why? I’m selfish because I so longed for another story of Fitz and Fool, another book to spend my time immersed in their world. And yet I feel cruel because I know how these stories go. Poor Fitz, things never fare well for him. So to wish for more stories, I almost feel like I am intruding on his peace, and wishing him more pain. I love Fitz, how can I wish his story to continue when I know that it’s liable to just bring him more heartache and sorrow and maybe even physical pain as well? That said, it is so freakin worth it. This is fiction. Heart-wrenching, gut punching, rip your heart at times, fiction.<br /><br />Once again, Hobb has delivered a fabulous story. And of course, her characters and the way readers form an emotional attachment to them is such a strength of her writing. Rarely do I feel so emotionally invested in a characters plight as I do when I read a book by Hobb. And this is no exception. Hobb’s books may not be as fast paced as some others, but the introspective look at her characters makes them as gripping as anything else I have ever read.<br /><br />This has a stronger feeling of “home” than any of the other books. It is set almost entirely at Withywoods, the home where Fitz has lived in with Molly since we last saw them at the end of the Tawny Man trilogy. Fitz’s life has a much more settled and domestic pace. He has done all he can to avoid Buckkeep Castle, Chade and all the machinations involved in being a bastard of the royal family. And he’s successful at that. At least for a while, at least until mysterious messengers arrive (and disappear), plunging poor ol’ Fitz back into his old ways of life as his only way to protect his future.<br /><br />In addition to Fitz’s POV, we also get a new character POV in Fool’s Assassin. This character is quite a special individual and brings a new perspective on pretty much everything. She is reasonable, honorable, quite intriguing and for fear of spoilers, I’m saying nothing beyond that I love what she brings to the story and I really look forward to reading about her again in the next book.<br /><br />My final comment/disclosure/forewarning: I know not everyone is a fan of cliffhangers. I know many people are more accepting of them when they know they are coming. So here it is, your warning that when you get to the end of Fool’s Assassin, the first thing you are liable to do is look up the expected publication date for the next book (which has not been announced yet, at least not at the time of writing this review). Personally, I was quite happy with it. I felt Fool’s Assassin told the beginning story of the trilogy. The course of events in this book are essential for setting up and understanding the larger story that we are just beginning to glimpse, and are waiting for in the next book. It took Fitz from his quiet retired life back into the maelstrom of all things Farseer.:Magic, intrigue, assassinations, prophesy. And heartache. Poor Fitz. I look forward to reading more of you in the next one.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7244860232399432833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nqsV0kLSLCO2ERlnsmXp2zL9+PIBEuWAx+dBw8wGHYL+vEHK7CnQ3eazAcqo72gqihse0Cjw/5xfLAaejIUk6A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gDpGeY7kqWHlDpgDH6S1bIQD3TmjqZJR73Ln4c+1wazgLRJhIB9Vn7WsgK4FLjSdPOU7G4pLiE13uaC8jzb4xg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">About Robin Hobb</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1397885202p3/25307.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">Robin Hobb
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

80,265
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15443386860455126808">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText15443386860455126808" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15443386860455126808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
